SEMESTER 5 
 
CHEMICAL ENGINEERING

 
 
SEMESTER S5 
MASS TRANSFER OPERATIONS II 
Course Code 
PCCHT501 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCHT403 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart fundamental concepts of mass transfer operations such as 
distillation, liquid extraction, leaching and membrane separation processes.  
2. To explain how to quantify, formulate, and solve engineering problems 
involving different mass transfer operations like distillation, liquid-liquid 
extraction, leaching and membrane separation processes. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Distillation: Vapour-Liquid Equilibria, boiling- point   diagram   and  
equilibrium   curves, relative volatility, application of Raoult’s law. 
Distillation methods- flash distillation, Simple distillation, Steam distillation, 
Fractionation of binary mixtures, Principle of fractionation, Fractionation in 
plate columns, condensers and reboilers. Material and energy balance. 
Problem solving in distillation using EXCEL / Matlab / SCILAB/ PYTHON 
etc. – only for self study / microproject / assignment 
11 
2 
Design of   fractionation   column: McCabe - Thiele   method - basic 
assumptions, feed quality and feed line, number of plates, feed plate location, 
total reflux, minimum reflux , optimum reflux, plate efficiency, cold reflux 
and  open steam. 
Ponchon–Savarit method: Enthalpy composition diagrams, Concept of net 
flow and difference point, Ponchon–Savarit method– material and enthalpy 
balance, number of plates, feed plate location, minimum reflux conditions. 
13 

 
 
Rectification in packed columns, height of packed towers. Azeotropic and 
Extractive distillation (qualitative treatment only). 
Problem solving in distillation using EXCEL / Matlab / SCILAB/ PYTHON 
etc. – only for self study / microproject / assignment 
3 
Extraction –applications, ternary   equilibria   on   triangular coordinate 
system, mixture rule, distribution curve, selectivity, choice   of   solvent. 
Single-stage   and   multistage   extraction operations - Calculations   for  
immiscible   systems   and   partially miscible systems. 
Construction and working of mixer -settler cascades, sieve-tray columns, 
agitated towers, pulse    columns and centrifugal extractors. 
10 
4 
Leaching – Rate of leaching, factors affecting rate of leaching.  Working 
principles of leaching equipment- Shank’s system- thickeners, classifiers and 
moving bed leaching equipment. Leaching equilibrium - constant underflow 
- variable underflow Single stage and multistage leaching. 
Membrane separation processes – classification – types of membranes: 
flat, spiral wound, hollow fibre -concentration polarization – ultrafiltration. 
10

SEMESTER 5 
CHEMICAL TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PCCHT502 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Familiarize students with chemical industry operations. It helps the student to develop 
new chemical products and processes, test processing equipment and instrumentation, 
gather data, and monitor quality. 
2. Reveals knowledge about operations of industries such as raw materials and products, 
unit operations and processes, engineering problems related to operations and 
marketing strategies currently followed in chemical industries, etc. 
3. Enable the students to do research, design, and construct safe, sustainable machinery 
to produce a wide range of valuable items. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to chemical industries:-Classification of chemical Industries 
Manufacture of sulphuric acid:- DCDA process, phosphoric acid - wet 
processes and electric furnace process. Chlor-alkali industries:- soda ash, 
caustic soda, chlorine. 
9 
2 
Fertilizer industries:–Ammonia, urea, single super phosphate and triple 
super phosphate. Natural product industries – Soap and detergents, 
glycerine, pulp and paper, sugar, oiland fats, starch, ethyl alcohol by 
fermentation. 
9 

 
 
3 
Petroleum refining:- Chemical composition of crude, petroleum refinery 
products, atmospheric distillation unit, octane number. Refinery conversion 
processes - pyrolysis, catalytic cracking process-fluidized bed and moving 
bed type, reforming. 
9 
4 
Petrochemicals:–Manufacture of acetylene, butadiene and phenol-cumene 
process. Polymerization industries:- polyethylene, polypropylene, PVC, 
polyamides-nylon6 and nylon 6,6, and polyester synthetic fibers.  
9

SEMESTER 5 
CHEMICAL REACTION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PCCHT503 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCHT303 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Enable students to apply the principles of chemical kinetics to describe the rates of 
chemical reactions for isothermal and non-isothermal reactions. 
2. Equip the students with fundamental knowledge for the design of different types of 
ideal reactors, including batch, continuous-stirred tank reactors (CSTR), plug-flow 
reactors (PFR for single and multiple reactions. 
3. Impart the concepts such as residence time distribution (RTD) and models 
required to analyze and design real reactors. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of chemical reaction engineering: Classification of chemical 
reactions, Variables affecting the rate of reaction, Definition of reaction 
rate. Kinetics of homogeneous reactions: Concentration-dependent and 
Temperature-dependent terms of rate equation, Temperature dependency 
from Arrhenius law, Collision theory, and transition state theory (no 
derivation). 
Interpretation of batch reactor data: Evaluation of rate equation by 
integral and differential methods of analysis for constant volume and 
variable volume systems. 
Problem 
solving 
in 
chemical 
kinetics 
using 
11  

 
 
EXCEL/Matlab/SCILAB/PYTHON etc. – only for self 
study/microproject/assignment. 
2 
Introduction to reactor design: Classification of reactors. 
Ideal reactors for a single reaction: Ideal batch reactor, Steady state mixed 
flow reactor, Steady state plug flow reactor. 
Design for single reactions: Size comparison of single reactors, 
Multiple reactor systems, Plug flow reactor in series and parallel, equal-
sized mixed reactors in series, mixed flow reactors of different sizes in 
series, determination of the best system for a given conversion.  
Recycle reactor,Auto catalytic reactions. 
Design for multiple reactions: Reactions in parallel, contacting patterns 
for reactions in parallel, qualitative discussion about product distribution of 
series reactions. 
Problem solving in ideal  reactors and recycle reactor using 
EXCEL/Matlab/SCILAB/PYTHON etc. – only for self 
study/microproject/assignment. 
11  
3 
Non isothermal reactor design: Temperature and pressure effects, single 
reactions, Heat of reaction from thermodynamics, heat of reaction and 
temperature, equilibrium constants from thermodynamics. General graphical 
design procedure, optimum temperature progression. Heat effects: adiabatic 
operations and non-adiabatic operations, Multiple Steady States in CSTR.  
Problem solving in non-isothermal reactors using 
EXCEL/Matlab/SCILAB/PYTHON etc. – only for self 
study/microproject/assignment. 
11 
4 
Non ideal reactors: Basics of nonideal flow, Residence time distribution 
studies - C, E & F curves and their relationships. Conversion in nonideal 
reactors, RTD in ideal reactors: Plug flow reactors, single CSTR.  Laminar 
flow reactor. Models for nonideal flow: dispersion model and tanks in 
series model. 
Problem solving in RTD, conversion in real reactors and models for 
nonideal flow in reactors using 
EXCEL/Matlab/SCILAB/PYTHON etc. – only for self 
study/microproject/assignment. 
 
11

SEMESTER 5 
CHEMICAL ENGINEERING DESIGN-I 
Course Code 
PBCHT504 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:1 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCHT205, PBCHT304, 
PCCHT402 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To give undergraduates a foundation in designing equipment used in process industries 
for heat transfer and evaporation operations. 
2. To familiarise using codes and standards for designing process equipment. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Thermal design of double pipe heat exchanger: Constructional features - 
Calculation of heat transfer area – estimation of heat transfer coefficient – 
calculation of the size of double pipe – pressure drop estimation in double 
pipe flow. 
Thermal design of shell and tube heat exchanger: Constructional features 
– baffles and pass partition – TEMA nomenclature – routing of fluids - 
Calculation of heat transfer area – estimation of tube bundle size - estimation 
of overall heat transfer coefficient using Bell’s method – pressure drop in 
shell side and tube side. 
Thermal design of shell and tube condensers for single component 
isothermal condensation of saturated vapours in the shell. Estimation of 
heat transfer area – Estimation of bundle size and shell diameter - estimation 
of in-shell condensation coefficients using Dukler charts/Nusselt equation – 
estimation of overall heat transfer coefficient. 
18 

 
 
2 
Thermal design of evaporators: 
Estimation of heat transfer area in single effect and multiple 
effect(double/triple effect forward feed only) evaporators with negligible 
boiling point rise   
Effect of boiling point elevation in evaporator calculation.  Constructional 
features and design of short tube calandria evaporator, long tube evaporator, 
and forced circulation evaporator. 
Mechanical design of process equipment: Design of thin-walled pressure 
vessels as per IS 2825 –Shells subject to internal and external pressure- flat 
ends, ends concave to pressure, and convex to pressure: domed ends and 
conical ends. 
18 
 
Suggestions on Project Topics 
 Identify a tubular exchanger in a plant and design the exchanger. The design shall include the 
following: 
a. Selection of exchanger type with justification 
b. Selection of material of construction for various parts, its specification with 
approximate cost data. 
c. Obtain/Prepare physical properties for the fluids in the operating range required for 
design. 
d. Manual sizing- First Design. 
e. Use computational tools to optimize the first design. 
f. Prepare design data sheet as per standards. 
 
 Identify a process that uses different types of evaporators. Choose a suitable evaporator and 
design it. The design shall include the following: 
g. Selection of evaporator type with justification 
h. Selection of material of construction for various parts, its specification with 
approximate cost data. 
i. 
Obtain/Prepare physical properties for the fluids in the operating range required for 
design. 
j. 
Manual sizing- First Design. 
k. Use computational tools to optimize the first design. 
l. 
Prepare design data sheet as per standards. 
 

 
 
 Conduct the mechanical design of tubular exchangers and evaporators as per Indian Standards/ 
ASME and prepare drawings.

End Semester Examination Marks (ESE) 
 
Total 
Two numerical questions will be given from each module, out of which one 
should be answered. The questions in each module shall be from different 
topics. Each question carries 20 marks.  
(2x20 = 40 marks) 
40 
 
The questions should be clear regarding the type of equipment and its alignment if 
any, operating conditions, and materials handled. Data required for design such as 
equilibrium data and physical properties in case it cannot be obtained from 
handbook/data book shall be provided with the question. 
Question paper should contain instruction as given below: 
• Assume any missing data suitably.  
• Apart from scientific calculators the following books and data books are 
permitted for the exam (Photostat copies of the books are not permitted except the 
item no.3 and item no.4): 
1. Steam tables 
2. Perry’s Handbook 
3. Attested copies or original of IS Codes (2825, 1730, 4049) 
4. Attested copies of Dühring's charts, Nomographs, charts and tables used in 
design taken from TEMA standard/other editions of Handbook. The copies 

 
 
should be attested by the course faculty concerned or as directed by 
university. 
• No other textbooks or materials such as handouts, printed notes etc. are permitted 
for the exam.

SEMESTER S5 
BIOCHEMICAL ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PECHT521 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To understand the fundamental aspects of Biochemical engineering 
2. 
To develop the kinetics of enzyme catalyzed reactions  
3. 
To acquire comprehensive knowledge of metabolic pathways, bioreactors and                           
biosensors 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Micro Biology, Cell 
theory, Structure of 
cells, 
Cell 
fractionation, 
protest kingdom and their distinguishing characteristics. Chemicals of life: 
repetitive 
and 
non-repetitive 
biopolymers 
- 
lipids, 
sugars 
and 
polysaccharides, amino acids and proteins. Protein structure 
nucleotides RNA and DNA. 
 
 
6 
2 
Kinetics of Enzyme catalyzed reactions: simple enzyme kinetics with one or 
two substrates, Michaelis - Menten Kinetics, Evaluation of parameters in 
Michaelis – Menten equation, Substrate activation and inhibition, 
Modulation and regulation of enzyme activity – competitive and 
uncompetitive inhibition. Enzyme specificity and enzyme specificity 
hypotheses. Enzymes of industrial importance. Immobilized enzyme 
technology: enzyme immobilization, medical and analytical applications of 
immobilized enzymes. Batch cultivation - growth cycle (lag, exponential, 
 
10 

 
 
stationery and death phase) 
3 
Metabolic pathways and energetics of the cell: Metabolic reaction 
coupling: ATP, ADP and NAD. Embden-Meyerhof pathway (EMP), 
Pentose phosphate cycle, Respiration - TCA cycle. Transport across cell 
membranes - passive transport, active transport and facilitated diffusion. 
Transport phenomena in Bio process system-Gas-liquid mass transfer in 
cellular system - basic mass transfer concepts - rates of metabolic oxygen 
utilization  
10 
4 
Biochemical reactors-specifications Continuous stirred tank bioreactor, 
bubble column bioreactor, Airlift bioreactors, Fluidized bed bioreactors, 
Packed bed bioreactors, and photo bioreactors. Types of reactors for 
sterilization. Fermentation technology, medium formulation, design and 
operation of a typical aseptic, aerobic fermentation process. Concept of 
biosensors. Physical and chemical sensors, gas analysis sensors, On-line 
sensors and offline sensors. 
 
10

SEMESTER S5  
OIL AND NATURAL GAS ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PECHT522 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To bring an optimal balance between natural gas production, natural gas processing 
and gas transportation, an extensive treatise on natural gas engineering, both upstream 
and gas refining processes with key equipment and facility design. 
2. Awareness of the current status of production of natural gas through unconventional 
sources/technics and the applications of natural gas. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Fundamentals of petroleum geology and exploration:- Introduction, 
origin, formation, geological occurrence and characteristics of oil and natural 
gas. 
Source Rocks, 
Reservoir Rocks, 
and Caprocks: 
Definition, 
Characteristics, Classification and nomenclature, Concept of Shale oil, 
Reservoir. Properties, Hydrocarbon migration, Petroleum Exploration. 
9 
2 
Conventional natural gas:- Associated gas, non-associated gas, Gas 
condensate. Unconventional production of natural gas: Coal bed methane, 
Natural gas hydrate, shale gas and tight gas sands.  
Coal bed methane - Introduction, present status, formation and properties of 
coal bed methane.  
Natural Gas Hydrate - Concepts and Structures, Evaluation and Prediction, 
Production Techniques.  
9 

 
 
Shale Gas - Exploration, Production - Drilling and completion. 
Separation and Processing: Gas and liquid separation – internal construction 
of separators, types of separators, factors affecting separation, separator 
design, stage separation, low temperature separation. 
3 
Dehydration of Natural gas: Water content of natural gas streams, hydrate 
control in gas production, dehydration systems - Glycol dehydration and 
Solid desiccant dehydration. 
Acid gas removal: Metal oxide process, Slurry process, Amine process, 
Carbonate washing process, Methanol based process and Sulphur recovery 
process.  
Compression of Natural Gas: Types of Compressors, Selection of 
reciprocating 
and 
centrifugal 
compressors, 
Thermodynamics 
of 
Compressors, Compression calculations. 
9 
4 
Gas flow measurement: Fundamentals, Methods of measurements, Orifice 
meters equation, turbine meters, Selection, Recording charts, Uncertainties in 
flow. 
Gas Gathering, Transportation and Storage: Gas Gathering System, Steady 
State and Unsteady  
State Flow in Pipelines, Transmission of Natural Gas, Specifications. 
Underground Storage and Conservation of Natural Gas.  
Liquefied Natural Gas: Gas treating before liquefaction- Liquefaction cycles- 
Storage of LNG, Transportation- Regasification and cold utilization of LNG. 
Economics - Plant efficiency - Safety and environmental considerations. 
9

sweetening.

SEMESTER S5 
POLYMER TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PECHT523 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart the basic concepts of polymer technology, 
2. To develop understanding about the different polymers as an engineering material. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to polymers-monomer, functionality, classification of polymer 
based on source, structure, application, thermal behaviour, mode of 
polymerization. Kinetics of polymerisation– addition polymerization and 
condensation polymerisation – free radical polymerization – anionic and 
cationic polymerization.  
Copolymerisation. Different types of copolymers – Characteristic features. 
Methods of polymerization – bulk, solution, suspension and emulsion 
polymerization. 
8  
2 
Molecular weight of polymers – weight average and number average 
molecular weight – sedimentation and viscosity average molecular weights. 
Experimental methods for molecular weight determination – end group 
analysis, light scattering method – viscometry (Ostwald viscometer) intrinsic 
viscosity. Molecular weight distribution curve.  
Factors affecting polymer properties – crystallinity – orientation treatment – 
solubility of polymers – glass transition temperature – types of polymer 
degradation – effect of reinforcement on the properties. 
10  

 
 
Properties of polymers – rheology- viscous flow – apparent viscosity – 
rubber like elasticity – stress strain behaviour of elastomers – viscoelasticity 
– stress relaxation and creep – measurement of rheological properties – melt 
flow index (MFI) – capillary rheometers. 
Estimation of tensile strength of polymers.  
3 
Manufacture, properties and applications of polymers:  
Thermoplastics– ABS, acrylics, cellulose acetate, fluoropolymers (PTFE), 
nylons, polycarbonate, PVC, PE, PP, PS, polyurethanes.  
Thermosetting plastics– epoxy, phenol formaldehyde, urea formaldehyde, 
polyesters, silicones.  
Bioplastics – Poly lactic acid (PLA).  
Elastomers- Butyl rubber –Nitrile rubber. 
9  
4 
Addictives for polymer processing - effect of additives used – plasticizers – 
colourants – heat stabilizers - antioxidants – ultraviolet absorbers – antistatic 
agents – flame retardants – blowing agents – lubricants and fillers. 
Plastic processing – injection moulding, compression moulding, calendaring, 
blow moulding, extrusion, thermoforming, wet, dry and melt spinning 
methods for fibres, vulcanization of rubber.  
General study of elastomer processing - brief description of compounding 
methods. 
9

Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The objective is to impart, a basic knowledge in project planning, plant process design, 
economic evaluation and financial control. 
2. To describe the importance of process development and process engineering to students. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Classification of Projects, Scope of Project engineering - the 
role of project engineer. 
Development of project: R&D, TEFR, Importance of Laboratory 
development of new process – Bench scale experiments – pilot plant studies 
– Semi-commercial plant. 
Process engineering: Conceptual process design- Preliminary process 
design- Detailed process design (FEED).  Flow diagrams – Plot plans - 
Engineering design and drafting (Detailed Engineering). 
Plant location and site selection, Preliminary data for construction of 
projects. 
10 
2 
Planning and scheduling of projects: use of bar chart, PERT/ CPM - 
Critical path calculations.   
Site development:  Foundation – Erection and site fabrication – 
Construction – Insulation – Start up and commissioning – Trial runs – 
Guarantee run and hand over 
8 

 
 
3 
. Company formation- Process license – Technology Transfer – Statutory 
sanctions.  
Contracts and Contractors: Introduction, detailing of scope of work, 
factors in selecting scope of work, Type of contracts- Factors in selecting 
type of contract, contractor selection 
8 
4 
 Selection of process equipments: Standard versus special equipment 
selection criteria, specification sheets. Scope of piping engineering, pipe 
sizing technique, Codes and standards, Piping design, Safety in plant 
design.  
Project financing: Means of finance, Financial institutions, special schemes, 
Financial institutions in India, key financial indicators and ratios of new 
projects 
10

SEMESTER S5 
NUMERICAL METHODS FOR PROCESS ENGINEERS  
Course Code 
PECHT526 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The course is designed to give an overview of numerical methods to students. 
2. The course aims at giving adequate exposure to methods for 
numerically solving algebraic and transcendental equations, 
system 
of 
linear 
and 
non-linear 
equations, 
polynomial 
interpolation, differential and partial differential equations. 
3. To help students to implement these solutions using Excel/ MATLAB or any 
relevant programming environments. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Motivation and Applications, Accuracy and precision, 
Errors, Sources of errors, Significant digits and Numerical instability - 
Numerical solution of polynomial and transcendental equations -
Bracketing methods: Bisection method –Regula-Falsi method -Open 
methods:  Newton-Raphson method - Fixed-point iteration - Solution of 
polynomial and transcendental equations using Excel/ MATLAB 
(Assignments/ Micro project only) 
8 
2 
Solutions of system of linear algebraic equations: Direct methods –
Gauss Elimination and Gauss - Jordan methods - Crout’s reduction 
method - error analysis - iterative methods - Jacobi’s iteration - Gauss-
seidel iteration - the relaxation method - convergence analysis - solution 
8 

 
 
of system of nonlinear equations by Newton-Raphson method - Solution 
of 
linear/ 
nonlinear 
algebraic 
equations 
using 
Excel/ 
MATLAB(Assignments/ Micro project only) 
3 
Polynomial interpolation: finite difference operators: Gregory – 
Newton forward and backward interpolations -Stirling’s interpolation 
formula- Lagrange’s interpolation polynomial - divided differences 
Newton’s divided difference interpolation polynomial - error of 
interpolation – Interpolation using Excel/ MATLAB(Assignments/ Micro 
project only) 
Numerical differentiation:  differential formulas in the case of equally 
spaced points - numerical integration - trapezoidal and Simpson’s rules - 
Gaussian integration - errors of integration formulas- Differentiation and 
Integration using Excel/ MATLAB(Assignments/ Micro project only) 
9 
4 
Numerical solution of ordinary differential equations:  The Taylor 
series method - Euler and modified Euler methods - Runge–Kutta 
methods (4th order only) - Multistep methods - Milne’s predictor - 
corrector formulas - Adam-Bashforth & Adam-MoultonFormulas-
Solution of boundary value problems in ordinary differential equations- 
solution 
of 
ordinary 
differential 
equations 
using 
Excel/ 
MATLAB(Assignments/ Micro project only) 
Solution of partial difference equations:  Classification of PDE’s- 
finite difference methods for solving two-dimensional Laplace’s equation 
for a rectangular region - finite difference method of solving heat 
equation and wave equation with given initial and boundary conditions- 
solution 
of 
partial 
differential 
equations 
using 
Excel/ 
MATLAB(Assignments/ Micro project only) 
11

SEMESTER S5 
CORROSION ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PECHT527 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To enlighten the engineering students about the scope and cost of corrosion. 
2. To make them understand the various types of corrosion under normal to severe corrosive 
environments in manufacturing industrial sectors.   
3. To develop the skills among the students about corrosion testing of materials and to 
familiarize the students in selection of materials, corrosion monitoring and prevention.  
4. To develop the specialized skills in corrosion control in different engineering materials and 
industries. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Definition and principles of corrosion: Definition and importance of 
corrosion, Corrosion engineering – scope in industries, Cost of corrosion, 
corrosion damage, classification of corrosion, Principles of corrosion 
phenomenon: Corrosion rate expressions, Electrochemical aspects – 
electrochemical reactions, polarization, passivity, Environmental effects–
effect of oxygen and oxidisers, velocity, concentration, temperature, galvanic 
coupling, Metallurgical and other aspects-metallic properties, economic 
considerations, importance of corrosion inspection. 
9 
2 
Forms of corrosion: Different forms of corrosion: Galvanic or two metal 
corrosion, Crevice corrosion, Pitting, Intergranular corrosion, Selective 
leaching, Erosion corrosion, Stress corrosion, Hydrogen damage. 
9 

 
 
3 
Corrosion testing and  monitoring and prevention: Corrosion testing and 
monitoring: Non-electrochemical and electrochemical methods: potentiostat, 
Tafel 
extrapolation, 
linear 
polarization, 
galvanostat, 
impedance 
spectroscopy, thermogravimetric technique, salt spray test, weight change 
measurements, Corrosion prevention: Materials selection, alteration of 
environment, design, cathodic protection and anodic protection, coatings. 
9 
4 
Corrosion and its control in different engineering materials and 
industries: Corrosion and its control in different engineering materials: 
concrete structures, duplex, super duplex stainless steels, ceramics, 
composites and polymers. Corrosion and its control in industries: Power, 
Process, Petrochemical, ship building, marine and fertilizer industries. 
Corrosion auditing in industries, Corrosion map of India. 
9

Prerequisites (if any) 
Basic courses in Heat Transfer, Mass 
Transfer and Reaction Engineering 
Course Type
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Enable the students to model chemical engineering problems. 
2. Equip the students with knowledge on modelling and simulation of 
processes and use various concepts such as linear algebra, differential 
calculus etc. to solve chemical engineering problems. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Mathematical formulation of the physical problems:- application of the 
law of conservationof mass, salt accumulation in stirred tank, starting of 
equilibrium still, solvent extraction in twostages, diffusion with chemical 
reaction, application of the law of conservation of energy,radial heat 
transfer through cylindrical conductors, heating a closed kettle, flow of heat 
froma fin. 
Problems in mathematical modelling of reactor/extractor/fins/diffuser using 
MATLAB/ SIMULINK/ DWSIM- only for self study/project/assignment 
9 
2 
Analytical (explicit) solution of ordinary differential equations 
encountered in chemical engineering problems:- first order differential 
equations, method of separation of variables, equations solved by 
integration factors, certain examples involving mass and energy balances 
and reaction kinetics, second order differential equations, non-linear 
9 

 
 
equations, linear equations, simultaneous diffusions and chemical reaction 
in a tubular reactor, continuous hydrolysis of tallow in a spray column. 
Formulation of partial differential equations, unsteady state heat conduction 
in one dimension, mass transfer with axial symmetry, continuity equations, 
boundary conditions, function specified, derivative specified and mixed 
conditions, iterative solution of algebraic equations - Jacobi s method, 
Gauss- Seidel method and successive order relaxation (S.O.R) method. 
Solution of ODE and PDE and develop performance equation of   tubular 
reactor, unsteady state heat conduction of given system using MATLAB/ 
SIMULINK/ DWSIM- only for self study/project/assignment 
3 
The difference operator:- properties of the difference operator, difference 
tables and other difference operators, linear finite difference equations, the 
complimentary solution and particular solution, simultaneous linear 
differential equations, non-linear finite difference equations, analytical 
solution. Solution of the following type of problems by finite difference 
method - calculation of the number of plates required for absorption 
column, calculation of the number of theoretical plates required for 
distillation column, number of steps required for a counter-current 
extraction and leaching operations. 
Finding number of plates/trays in absorption column/ distillation column 
using modern software tools- only for self study/ assignments/ projects 
9 
4 
Application of statistical methods:- propagation of errors of experimental  
data, parameter estimation of algebraic equations encountered in heat and 
mass transfer, kinetics and thermodynamics by the method of averages, 
linear least squares and weighted linear least square methods, design of 
experiments: factorial, fractional factorial methods. 
Doing simple experiments in laboratory and perform statistical analysis by 
tools like EXCEL/MINITAB/R/PYTHON – only for self study/ assignments/ 
projects. 
9

Criteria for Evaluation (Evaluate and Analyse): 20 marks 
 
1. Problem Definition (4 points) 
1. Clearly defines the real-world problem in process engineering. 
2. Examine and identifies relevant contextual factors. 
2. Problem Analysis (4 points) 
1. Break-down and presents a well-reasoned solution approach. 
2. Compare and justify the proposed solutions with evidence and logical reasoning. 
3. Evaluate (4 points) 
1. Thoroughly evaluate the proposed solutions. 
2. Considers feasibility and practical implications. 
4. Implementation of software (4 points) 
1. Select the most feasible solution by implementing the proposed solutions. 
2. Demonstrates proficiency in relevant software. 
5. Conclusion (K4- 2 points, K5 – 2 points) 
1. Summarizes findings and insights. (K4) 
2. Reflects critical thinking and informed decision-making. (K5)

SEMESTER S5 
CHEMICAL REACTION ENGINEERING LAB  
Course Code 
PCCHL507 
CIE Marks 
50 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
0:0:3:0

50 
Credits 
2 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCHT503 
Course Type 
Lab 
 
Course Objectives: Chemical Reaction Engineering Lab familiarize students with main type 
of chemical reactors. Students are able to analyze the experimental data to obtain the reaction 
rate expression (reaction order and specific reaction rate constant). 
1. Operate lab equipments like Batch, CSTR and PFR reactors 
2. Analyze the concentration versus time data and determine the specific rate constant 
and the order of the reaction. 
3. Compare theoretical and experimental conversions in a CSTR and PFR. 
4. Estimate RTD and model parameters in a CSTR, PFR and packed bed reactor

4 
Packed Bed Reactor  
5 
RTD Studies in a Packed Bed Reactor  
6 
RTD Studies in CSTR  
7 
RTD Studies in PFR  
8 
Combined Flow Reactor

Continuous Assessment (25 Marks) 
1. Preparation and Pre-Lab Work (7 Marks) 
 Pre-Lab Assignments: Assessment of pre-lab assignments or quizzes that test 
understanding of the upcoming experiment. 
 Understanding of Theory: Evaluation based on students’ preparation and 
understanding of the theoretical background related to the experiments. 
2. Conduct of Experiments (7 Marks) 
 Procedure and Execution: Adherence to correct procedures, accurate execution 
of experiments, and following safety protocols. 
 Skill Proficiency: Proficiency in handling equipment, accuracy in 
observations, and troubleshooting skills during the experiments. 
 Teamwork: Collaboration and participation in group experiments. 

 
 
3. Lab Reports and Record Keeping (6 Marks) 
 Quality of Reports: Clarity, completeness and accuracy of lab reports. Proper 
documentation of experiments, data analysis and conclusions. 
 Timely Submission: Adhering to deadlines for submitting lab reports/rough 
record and maintaining a well-organized fair record. 
4. Viva Voce (5 Marks) 
 Oral Examination: Ability to explain the experiment, results and underlying 
principles during a viva voce session. 
Final Marks Averaging: The final marks for preparation, conduct of experiments, 
viva, and record are the average of all the specified experiments in the syllabus. 
Evaluation Pattern for End Semester Examination (50 Marks) 
1. Procedure/Preliminary Work/Design/Algorithm (10 Marks) 
 Procedure Understanding and Description: Clarity in explaining the procedure 
and understanding each step involved. 
 Preliminary Work and Planning: Thoroughness in planning and organizing 
materials/equipment. 
 Algorithm Development: Correctness and efficiency of the algorithm related 
to the experiment. 
 Creativity and logic in algorithm or experimental design. 
2. Conduct of Experiment/Execution of Work/Programming (15 Marks) 
 Setup and Execution: Proper setup and accurate execution of the experiment 
or programming task. 
3. Result with Valid Inference/Quality of Output (10 Marks) 
 Accuracy of Results: Precision and correctness of the obtained results. 
 Analysis and Interpretation: Validity of inferences drawn from the experiment 
or quality of program output. 
 
 
 
 
 
 

 
 
4. Viva Voce (10 Marks) 
 Ability to explain the experiment, procedure results and answer related 
questions 
 Proficiency in answering questions related to theoretical and practical aspects 
of the subject. 
5. Record (5 Marks) 
 Completeness, clarity, and accuracy of the lab record submitted

SEMESTER 6 
 
CHEMICAL ENGINEERING

 
SEMESTER S6 
CHEMICAL ENGINEERING DESIGN II 
Course Code 
PCCHT601 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:1:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
4 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PCCHT205,PCCHT302, 
PCCHT303, PCCHT403, 
PCCHT501 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To give a foundation for the undergraduates in the design of equipment used in process 
industries for distillation, gas absorption, liquid extraction and drying 
2. To familiarise mechanical design of tall equipment by applying basic principles of 
mechanics. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Process design of steady state isothermal binary component tray 
distillation columns (Sieve and valve tray): Estimation of theoretical 
number of stages using McCabe Thiele method –Tray design – tray 
efficiency - pressure drop, entrainment, downflow flooding and weeping. 
Process design of steady state isothermal packed bed absorption and 
stripping column for dilute systems without chemical reaction: Number 
of transfer units- height of transfer units – column diameter – packing 
height-liquid distribution-pressure drop. 
Process design of single solvent sieve tray extraction columns for 
immiscible system: Number of trays, sieve tray design, height of coalesced 
layer, Murphree efficiency. 
 
18  
2 
Design of Direct heat Rotary Dryers: Estimation of air quantity, drying 
 

 
temperature, Number of Transfer Units, Diameter of dryer, Length and hold 
up time. 
Mechanical design of tall pressure vessels: design of thin walled multi-
course pressure vessels as per IS 2825 – Estimation of thickness of shells 
subject to external loads (wind and seismic) – Design of skirt support for tall 
columns. 
18

(CIE: 40 marks, ESE: 60 marks)

End Semester Examination Marks (ESE)
Total
2 numerical questions will be given from each module, out of which 1 question 
should be answered. The questions in each module shall be from different topics. 
Each question carries 30 marks.  
(2x30 = 60 marks) 
60 
The questions should be clear in respect of type of equipment, operating conditions, 
materials handled and objective. Data required for design such as equilibrium data 
and physical properties in case it cannot be obtained from handbook/data book shall 
be provided with the question. 
Question paper should contain instruction as given below: 
• Assume any missing data suitably.  
• Apart from scientific calculators the following books and data books are 
permitted for the exam (Photostat copies of the books are not permitted 
except the item no.2): 
1. Steam tables 
 

 
2. Perry’s Handbook (Original or attested bound copy of Chapters 
1,2,3,4,5,6,10,11,12,13,14 &15) 
3. Attested copies or original of IS Codes (2825, 1730, 4049) 
4. Attested copies of Psychrometric charts, Nomographs, charts and tables 
used in design taken from other editions of Handbook/References.  
5. Attested copy of Sieve tray hydraulics and sieve tray mass transfer for 
liquid extraction 
from ‘Mass Transfer Operations’ by Robert E. Treybal, pg 532-538. 
(The copies should be attested by the course faculty concerned or as 
directed by university.) 
No other textbooks or materials such as handouts, printed notes etc. are permitted 
for the exam.

SEMESTER S6 
TRANSPORT PHENOMENA 
Course Code 
PCCHT602 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBCHT304, 
PCCHT402, PCCHT403 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart knowledge in transport of momentum, heat and mass transport and provide 
insight into the dependence of temperature and pressure on the transport coefficients. 
2. To derive simple shell balances to formulate basic conservation equations of transport 
processes for solving selected engineering problems which can be solved analytically. 
3. To give basic axioms of conservation namely conservation of momentum, energy and 
mass. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Prediction of transport coefficients: viscosity, thermal conductivity and 
diffusivity. Momentum Transport – Viscosity and the mechanisms of 
momentum transfer, Generalization of Newton’s law of viscosity, pressure 
and temperature dependence of viscosity of gases and liquids, prediction of 
viscosity of gases: Rigid sphere model and rigorous models, Numerical 
problems. 
Energy Transport: Thermal conductivity and the mechanism of energy 
transport- prediction of thermal conductivity of gases, effect of temperature 
and pressure on thermal conductivity of gases, relationship between thermal 
conductivity and viscosity of gases. Thermal conductivity of solids, the 
relationship between thermal and electrical conductivity of solids, Numerical 
problems. 
 
11 

 
Diffusivity and the Mechanism of Mass Transport: Definition of 
concentrations, velocities and mass/molar fluxes, interrelationship between 
fluxes. Fick’s law of diffusion, kinetic theory of diffusion in gases at low 
density, theory of ordinary diffusion in liquids. Prediction of diffusivity of 
gases, the effect of temperature, pressure and composition on diffusivity, 
Numerical problems. 
2 
Shell momentum balance: boundary conditions - application of shell 
balance to simple flow systems - falling film -flow of a Newtonian fluid in 
between two slits formed by two flat plates, flow through tube - flow through 
annulus - flow of two adjacent immiscible fluids. 
General transport equations for momentum:  derivation of continuity 
equation and equation of motion in rectangular coordinates - Navier Stoke’s 
equation and Euler equation – transport equations in curvilinear coordinates 
(no derivation) - application of transport equations to steady flow problems - 
flow through tube - tangential annular flow - rotating liquid. 
11 
3 
Shell energy balance:  boundary conditions - application of shell balance to 
heat conduction problems - conduction with electric, nuclear and viscous 
heat sources, use of shell heat balances in variable thermal conductivity 
systems to derive temperature and heat flux profiles, cooling fins with 
insulated tip condition. Equations of energy in rectangular and curvilinear 
coordinates (no derivation) - application to steady state heat transfer 
problems - tangential flow in annulus with viscous heat generation – flow of 
nonisothermal film - transpiration cooling. 
11 
4 
Analogies between heat, mass and momentum transfer:  Shell mass 
balance - boundary conditions - diffusion through stagnant gas - diffusion 
with heterogeneous and homogeneous chemical reaction-diffusion and 
chemical reaction in porous catalyst – other similar diffusion problems, 
equation of continuity for binary mixtures in rectangular coordinates. 
11

SEMESTER S6 
PROCESS MODELLING AND SIMULATION 
Course Code 
PECHT631 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart the basic concepts of modelling of chemical processes 
2. To impart the basic concepts of simulation of chemical processes 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Definition of Modelling, Simulation, Advantages and 
limitations, Applications. Models and classification of models, Alternate 
classification of models, Mathematical modelling based on Transport 
phenomena, Basic concepts, Basic modelling principles, Energy 
equations, continuity equation, equation of motion, transport equations, 
equations of state, Equilibrium states and chemical kinetics. 
8 
2 
Mathematical models of Lumped Systems: Continuous flow tanks, 
Mixing vessel without reaction, Isothermal reactor with irreversible and 
reversible reaction. Non-isothermal steam jacketed reactor, Boiling-open 
and enclosed vessel, Batch distillation, Ideal binary distillation column -
Simulation using MATLAB/SciLab or any other process simulator 
(Assignments/ Microprojects only) 
10 
3 
Mathematical models of Distributed systems:  Jacketed tubular reactor, 
Counter current liquid-liquid double-pipe heat exchanger, Unsteady Heat 
conduction through a rod, Tubular permeation process, Gas absorber- 
Simulation using MATLAB/SciLab or any other process simulator 
(Assignments/ Microprojects only) 
10 
4 
Simulation of systems: Algorithm for solving Continuous flow tank, 
Isothermal CSTR in series, Non-isothermal CSTR, Binary distillation 
column. 
8

SEMESTER S6 
PETROLEUM REFINERY ENGINEERING 
Course Code 
PECHT 632 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
Nil 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. This course will present an overview of the modern, integrated petroleum refinery, its feed 
stocks, products and the processes employed to convert crude oil and intermediate streams 
into finished products 
2. This course provides major insights into both primary and secondary processes like 
Atmospheric Distillation, Vacuum Distillation, Cracking, Hydrocracking, Catalytic 
Reforming Processes for LOBS in a typical refinery. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Origin and composition- Origin and formation of crude oil. Oil exploration 
and drilling. Storage and transportation of crude oil and products. 
Classification, Composition and Evaluation of oil stock. Status of Petroleum 
industry in India. Classification of petroleum refinery. Fundamentals of 
Refinery economics, Refinery complexity index 
9 
2 
Preliminary and Primary petroleum processing-Impurities in crude oil, 
Dehydration and desalting of crude, Electric Desalter-, Process description, 
factors affecting the electric desalter. Pipe still furnaces and its operations. 
Distillation of crude- Prefractionator, Atmospheric topping unit, Vacuum 
distillation unit 
8 

 
3 
Secondary conversion process-Thermal Conversion process. Thermal 
cracking, Visbreaking, Coking (Delayed coking). Types and uses of 
petroleum coke. Catalytic conversion process-Catalytic cracking-Types of 
Catalyst. Process description of Fluid Catalytic cracking unit. Process 
variables. Latest developments in the catalytic cracking process. Process 
description and applications of Hydro cracking. 
9 
4 
Production of gasoline and treatment of Petroleum products- Catalytic 
reforming, Alkylation (Sulphuric acid alkylation), Isomerisation with 
Platinum catalyst. Hydrogen production in Refinery, Acid gas removal and 
Sulphur recovery units.   
Treatment of gasoline-Merox sweetening. Production and treatment of 
L.P.G. Diesel Hydro desulphurisation. Treatment of Kerosene- Edeleanu 
process. Production and treatment of Lube- Phenol extraction. Dewaxing 
methods- Chilling and pressing and MEK dewaxing. 
 Properties, test methods and uses of Refinery products such as L.P.G,   
Gasoline, Jet fuel, Kerosene, Diesel fuel, Lube oil and Bitumen. 
10

SEMESTER S6 
HETEROGENEOUS REACTIONS AND CATALYSIS  
Course Code 
PECHT633 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To explain basic principles and theories of heterogeneous catalysis, including adsorption, 
desorption, surface reactions, and diffusion processes. 
2. To develop an understanding of reaction kinetics in heterogeneous 
catalysis. 
3. To acquire skills in various techniques for catalyst preparation and characterisation. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Catalyst and catalytic reactors: Catalysts, types of catalysts, catalytic 
properties, steps in a catalytic reaction, adsorption equilibrium constant, 
desorption, surface reaction, synthesizing rate law, rate limiting step, 
Langmuir-Hinshelwood approach. Development of design equations for 
ideal mixed batch reactor, plug flow tubular reactor and perfectly mixed 
continuous stirred tank reactor for heterogeneous systems. Heterogeneous 
data analysis for reactor design 
9 
2 
Diffusion and reaction in porous catalysts: effective diffusivity, 
tortuosity-modelling of diffusion with reaction on a spherical catalysts. 
Thiele Modulus, internal effectiveness factor, Overall effectiveness factor. 
Estimation of diffusion and reaction limited regimes - Weisz - Prater 
criterion for internal diffusion, Mears criterion for external diffusion. 
9 

 
3 
Fluid Particle Reactions (Non catalytic):  Selection of a model: 
Unreacted core model for spherical particles of unchanging size, model 
development for diffusion through gas film, ash layer, and chemical 
reaction controls. Rate of reaction for shrinking spherical particles - 
chemical reaction controls, diffusion controls, application to design., 
9 
4 
Selection, design, and Preparation of catalysts:  Deposition, impregnation, 
precipitation, co-precipitation, and sol-gel formation. Characterization of 
catalysts- pore volume, pore size, and pore size distribution- Mercury 
porosimetry- Nitrogen desorption method- BET method. Thermogravimetric 
analysis- Differential thermal analysis- X-ray diffraction method- Electron 
microscopy- 
Scanning 
electron 
microscopy- 
Transmission 
electron 
microscopy- Atomic emission spectroscopy.  
9

SEMESTER S6 
FUEL CELL TECHNOLOGY 
Course Code 
PECHT634 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min.  
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To expose the students to the fundamental knowledge required in the development of fuel 
cells 
 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Fuel Cell, Brief History of fuel cells, Types of Fuel Cells, 
Fuel Cell and conventional processes – comparison, Energy & power 
relations, units, Application scenarios, Advantages and disadvantages. 
Overview of Fuel Cell Types: PAFC, PEMFC, AFC, MCFC, SOFC - Major 
Cell Components, Processes, Operating Conditions, and applications. 
General Thermodynamics: Enthalpy-Heat potential of fuel, Gibb's free 
energy-Work potential of fuel, Reversible voltage - NERNST Equation, 
Voltage and P, T and concentration dependence – examples, Faraday's Laws, 
Efficiency: thermodynamic, voltage and fuel.  
10  
2 
Reaction Kinetics: Electrochemical reaction fundamentals, electrode 
kinetics, Charge transfer and activations energy, Exchange current density - 
slow and fast reactions, Potential and equilibrium - galvanic potential, 
Reaction rate and potential - Butler Volmer equation & Tafel equation. 
9 
3 
Charge and Mass Transport: Charge transport resistances, voltage losses, 
Ionic and electronic conductivities, Ionic conduction in different FC 
9 

 
electrolytes: Aqueous, polymeric, and ceramic, Diffusive transport & voltage 
loss: Limiting current density, Nernstian and kinetic effect. Convective 
transport: flow channels, gas diffusion / porous layer, gas velocity, pressure, 
Flow channel configurations 
4 
Stack Design: Sizing of a Fuel Cell Stack, Stack Configuration, Uniform 
distribution of Reactants, Heat removal, Stack Clamping  
Fuel Cell System Design: Hydrogen-Oxygen Systems, Hydrogen-Air 
Systems, Fuel Cell Systems with Fuel Processor, System Efficiency 
8

SEMESTER S6 
PROCESS UTILITY AND PIPING ENGINEERING  
Course Code 
PECHT636 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs 30 Min 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. 
To classify the common process utility used in process industries. 
2. 
To develop an understanding of working of different process utility systems. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Process Utility Systems: Classification of process utility systems, 
Importance of process utilities in chemical industries and plants.  
Water as a utility in process industries: Sources of water, hard and soft 
water, methods of water treatment, recycle and conservation of water.  
Cooling Tower: Constructional details, Working, Types and performance 
evaluation. 
9 
2 
Introduction to Fuels:- Properties of Fuel oil, Coal and Gas, Storage, 
handling and preparation of fuels, Principles of Combustion, Combustion 
of Oil, Coal and Gas.  
Compressed air system: Types of air compressors, Compressor 
efficiency, Compressed air system components, Factors affecting the 
performance and efficiency of compressors.  
Vacuum Pumps: Types of vacuum pumps and their performance 
characteristics. 
9 
3 
Steam System: Steam and its importance, Properties of steam, Problems 
based on enthalpy calculation for wet steam, dry saturated steam, and 
superheated steam.  
8 

 
Boilers: Types of steam generators/boilers, Combustion in boilers, 
Performance evaluation, Analysis of losses, Feed water treatment, Blow 
down, Boilers Act.  
Steam handling and distribution: Steam distribution system, Assessment 
of steam distribution losses, Steam economy, Steam traps, Condensate and 
flash steam recovery system. Waste Heat Recovery: Classification, 
Advantages and applications, commercially viable waste heat recovery 
devices. 
4 
Refrigeration and Ventilation: Principles of refrigeration, vapour 
compression and vapour absorption refrigeration cycles, types of 
refrigerants and their importance. Production of cryogenic temperatures. 
Exhaust & Ventilation.  
Introduction to Piping: Classification of pipes, pipe materials, pipe sizing, 
pipe wall thickness, schedule number, codes and standards. Piping colour 
codes as per types of fluid passing through pipes. Piping Components: 
Pipes, Fittings, Flanges, Gaskets, and Valves. Pipe fittings: Functions and 
properties, types of pipe fittings and their selection. Gaskets: Functions and 
properties, types of gaskets and their selection. Valves: Types of valves. 
Piping insulation: Insulation materials, estimating thickness of insulation, 
critical thickness of insulation, optimal thickness of insulation. 
10

Course Objectives: 
1. Provide comprehensive and balanced understanding of essential link between 
synthetic fertilizer industries.  
2. Identify engineering problems in fertilizer manufacturing. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Overview of Fertilizer: Synthetic fertilizers, Classification of fertilizers, 
Role of essential Elements in plant Growth, Macro elements and Micro 
elements, Application of fertilizers considering Nutrient, Balance and types 
of crop. Development of fertilizer industry; Fertilizer production and 
consumption in India; Nutrient contents of fertilizers; Secondary nutrients;

fertilizers. 
8

properties, 
Manufacturing 
of 
Urea 
by 
10

neutralization. 
3 
Phosphatic and Pottasium Fertilizers:  Manufacture and application of 
MAP, DAP, Single Superphosphate, Triple super phosphate. Physical, 
chemical properties and uses of Potassium Chloride, Potassium nitrate, 
Potassium sulphate, Manufacturing of potassium chloride from sylvinite, 
Preparation of Potassium nitrate, Potassium sulphate. 
9 
4 
Miscellaneous Fertilizer and Bio Fertilizers:Introduction to complex and 
mixed fertilizers. Manufacturing of NPK, Ammonium Sulphate Phosphate 
(ASP), Calcium Ammonium Nitrate(CAN), Biofertilizers, Types of 
Biofertilizers, fixing biofertilizers, Phosphate-solubilizing biofertilizers, 
Preparation of a biofertilizers.

SEMESTER S6 
COMPUTATIONAL FLUID DYNAMICS 
Course Code 
PECHT635 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
5/3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min.  
Prerequisites (if any) 
PBCHT304 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Impart a solid understanding of the fundamental principles of fluid dynamics through 
governing equations, turbulence models and boundary conditions. 
2. Develop the ability to analyze and solve fluid flow problems using numerical techniques. 
3. Enable proficient use of computational tools to set up, run, and interpret simulations for a 
variety of fluid flow problems, ensuring application to real-world engineering scenarios and 
research projects. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction: Need of CFD as an analysis tool, Applications of CFD. CFD 
software packages and tools. CFD solution procedure: pre-processing, 
numerical solution – CFD solver, post-processing. Classification of partial 
differential equations (PDE) and boundary conditions: well-posed problems. 
Review of governing equations: Continuity equation, Momentum equation, 
Energy equation, Navier – Stokes equation, generic form of governing 
equations.   
9 
2 
Basic concepts of CFD: Introduction to discretization, Finite difference 
approximation of a derivative, discretization of differential equations using 
finite differences, consistency, convergence and stability (concepts alone), 
concept of explicit and implicit methods, Crank Nicholson scheme (FTCS 
only). 
9 

 
3 
Finite Volume Discretization: Diffusion problem, convection-diffusion 
problem, properties of discretization schemes – conservativeness, 
boundedness, transportiveness. Solution to discretized equations: TDMA, 
Jacobi, Gauss-Seidel, Gauss elimination methods. 
Detailed study of Navier stokes Equation-Solution of the Navier Stokes 
Equations. Grid arrangement-collocated and staggered grid. SIMPLE 
algorithm. 
9 
4 
Turbulence modelling: Need for turbulence modelling. Closure problem. 
Reynolds averaged Navier Stokes equation. Turbulence modelling. 
Multiphase flow modelling in CFD: Classification of multiphase flow, 
Industrial examples, Examples for multiphase reactors, Multiphase flow 
modelling approaches Eulerian-Lagrangian approach, Eulerian – Eulerian 
Approach, Volume of fluid approach. 
9 
 
Suggestions on Project Topics 
Assignment/Project: 20 Marks 
Students should evaluate and analyze a real-world problem, assess the proposed solutions, 
provide a conclusion on which solution is most appropriate for the problem, and implement 
the chosen solution using any computational tools like ANSYS, Open Foam, Matlab etc. 
Level: Analyze 
1. Problem Definition and Decomposition: 
 Clarity and Completeness (2 points): Evaluate the clarity and completeness of the 
problem definition. Are the objectives well-defined? Is the problem broken down into 
manageable sub-problems? 
 
Identification of Key Parameters (2 points): Assess the identification and justification of 
key parameters influencing the fluid dynamics problem. Are all relevant variables and 
boundary conditions considered? 
2. Analytical Approach: 
 
Methodological Soundness (1 points): Evaluate the soundness of the chosen analytical 
methods. Are the equations and principles correctly applied to the problem? 
 
Critical Analysis (1 points): Assess the depth of critical analysis in the approach. Are 
assumptions and limitations clearly stated and justified? 
 

 
3. Data Interpretation: 
 
Accuracy and Consistency (2 points): Evaluate the accuracy and consistency of the data 
interpretation. Are the results logically derived from the data? 
 
Comparison with Theoretical Predictions (2 points): Assess how well the results are 
compared with theoretical predictions or existing literature. Are discrepancies analyzed 
and explained? 
Level: Evaluate 
1. Simulation Setup and Execution: 
 
Appropriateness of CFD Tool (1 point): Evaluate the appropriateness of the chosen CFD 
tool for the problem at hand. Is the tool well-suited to model the specific fluid dynamics 
scenario? 
 
Simulation Accuracy and Robustness (2 points): Assess the accuracy and robustness of 
the simulation setup. Are the mesh, time steps, and convergence criteria appropriately 
chosen? 
2. Results Validation: 
 
Validation against Experimental Data (1 point): Evaluate the extent and rigor of 
validation against experimental or benchmark data. Are the validation methods 
appropriate and convincingly presented? 
 
Error Analysis (1 point): Assess the thoroughness of error analysis. Are sources of error 
identified and quantified? Are their impacts on the results discussed? 
3. Conclusions and Recommendations: 
 
Logical Consistency (1 point): Evaluate the logical consistency of the conclusions drawn 
from the analysis and simulation results. Are the conclusions supported by the data? 
 
Practical Implications and Recommendations (1 point): Assess the practical 
implications and recommendations based on the findings. Are the recommendations 
feasible and well-grounded in the analysis? 
4. Presentation and Communication: 
 
Clarity and Organization (1 point): Evaluate the clarity and organization of the project 
report or presentation. Is the information logically structured and easy to follow? 
 
Technical Writing and Visual Aids (2 points): Assess the quality of technical writing 
and the effectiveness of visual aids (graphs, charts, simulations). Are complex concepts 
clearly explained and visually supported?

SEMESTER S6 
PROCESS DYNAMICS AND CONTROL 
Course Code 
PBCHT604 
CIE Marks 
60 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
4 
ESE Marks 
40 
Credits 
3:0:0:1 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
4 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
 Sound knowledge in process control is very important for Chemical Engineers. Process control has 
become increasingly important in the process industries as a consequence of global competition, 
rapidly changing economic conditions, and more stringent environmental and safety regulations. 
Proper application of process control improves the safety and profitability of a process, while 
maintaining consistently the desired product quality. 
1. Model chemical engineering processes and analyze/predict their dynamics both for open-
(without control) and closed-loop (with control) cases. 
2. Develop control strategies and select the most appropriate input to manipulate, and totune 
controllers to meet/achieve process objectives. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to process dynamics and control: - definition of terms - 
Laplace transform - transform of simple functions - derivatives and integral 
- properties of Laplace transforms - final value theorem - initial value 
theorem - transition of transforms and functions – examples - inversion by 
partial fraction - solution of differential equations- linear open loop systems 
- first order systems - mercury thermometer, liquid level and mixing 
processes - response of these towards different types of forcing functions. 
(Study of dynamics by conducting experiments in above studied first order 
systems and  simulation in MATLAB/SCILAB- for self study/project) 
9 

 
2 
Systems in series: - interacting and non-interacting types and 
generalization of results. Linear open loop second order systems - 
manometer - response of these towards different types of forcing 
functions: step and sinusoidal functions.  Control valves- Characteristics- 
P, PI and PID Controllers - basic principles and transfer functions. 
(Study of dynamics by conducting experiments in above studied second 
order systems, simulation in MATLAB/SCILAB- Controllers/Control 
valve characteristics- forself study/project) 
9 
3 
Closed loop system: – feedback control- servo and regulator problems -
block diagram development –Block diagram reduction-Transient response of 
simple control systems - step response and offset. 
Introduction to stability of linear systems: - Routh- Hurwitz criterion for 
stability -Root locus technique-plotting root locus diagram. 
(Plottingroot 
locus 
diagrams 
and 
stability 
analysis 
using 
MATLAB/SCILAB/SIMULINK-for self study/project) 
9 
4 
Introduction to frequency response: - substitution rule – Bode diagram for 
first order systems - first order systems in series - bode stability criterion, 
gain margin and phase margin. 
Controller tuning:- Ziegler-Nichol’s method - comparison of closed loop 
responses for different controller settings. 
(Plotting 
Bode 
diagrams 
and 
stability 
analysis 
using 
MATLAB/SCILAB/SIMULINK-for self study/project) 
9 
 
Suggestion on Project Topics 
The students shall be directed to carry out any one of the projects listed below. 
1. Design and simulation of suitable temperature control system for stirred tank heater. 
2. Design and simulation of suitable level or flow control system for a single tank system. 
3. Design and simulationof suitable level or flow control system for a multi-tank system. 
4. Design and simulation of suitable control system to maintain product concentration in 
continuous stirred tank reactor. 
5. Design and simulation of a temperature control system for a continuous stirred tank reactor 
used in chemical process. 
6. Any other relevant project related to process dynamics and control. 
 

 
 
 
The completed project work should consist of following key components 
 
1. Fundamental Concept:  The dynamic behaviour of the process (Module 1) 
2. System Modelling: Develop a model for the selected system from fundamental 
conservation principles  (Module 1 and 2) 
3. Block Diagram development: Develop a feed back control system using the concept of 
block diagram development and reduction. (Module 3) 
4. Controller selection: Select a suitable controller for the process (Module 2 and 3) 
5. Simulation: Implement the system model and controller in MATLAB or Simulink and 
simulate the response. (Self -study) 
6. Stability analysis: Analyse the stability of the system using methods like Routh-Hurwitz 
Criterion, Root Locus method, Bode stability criterion etc. (Module 4) 
7. Controller tuning: Optimize the control parameter for desired performance using 
Ziegler- Nichols tuning. (Module 4) 
8. Validation by experimental data: Conduct experiment in the laboratory and evaluate the 
system performance with the experimental data (Conduct experiment in lab and obtain 
data for validation) 
9. Report preparation and oral presentation: Prepare a detailed report and presentation 
before the evaluation committee.

SEMESTER S6 
PROCESS UTILITIES  
Course Code 
OECHT611 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To classify the common process utility used in process industries. 
2. To develop an understanding of working of different process utility systems. 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Process Utility Systems: Classification of process utility systems, 
Importance of process utilities in chemical industries and plants.  
Water as a utility in process industries: Sources of water, hard and soft 
water, methods of water treatment. 
Cooling Tower: Constructional details, Working, Types and performance 
evaluation. 
9 
2 
Introduction to Fuels: Properties of Fuel oil, Coal and Gas, Storage, 
handling and preparation of fuels, Principles of Combustion, Combustion 
of Oil, Coal and Gas.  
Compressed air system: Types of air compressors, Compressor 
efficiency, Compressed air system components, Factors affecting the 
performance and efficiency of compressors.  
Vacuum Pumps: Types of vacuum pumps. 
9 
3 
Steam System: Steam and its importance, Properties of steam, wet steam, 
dry saturated steam, and superheated steam.  
Boilers: Types of steam generators/boilers, Combustion in boilers, 
9 

 
Performance evaluation, Analysis of losses, Feed water treatment, Blow 
down, Boilers Act.  
Steam handling and distribution: Steam distribution system, Assessment 
of steam distribution losses, Steam traps, Condensate and flash steam 
recovery system. Waste Heat Recovery: Classification.  
4 
Refrigeration and Ventilation: Principles of refrigeration, vapour 
compression and vapour absorption refrigeration cycles, types of 
refrigerants and their importance. Exhaust & Ventilation.  
Introduction to Piping: Classification of pipes, pipe materials, pipe sizing, 
schedule number, codes and standards. Piping Components: Pipes, Fittings, 
Flanges, Gaskets, and Valves.  
9

(CIE: 40 marks,ESE: 60 marks)

SEMESTER S6 
POLYMER SCIENCE AND ENGINEERING   
Course Code 
OECHT612 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To impart a comprehensive study of polymers and their classification, Molecular Weight 
and Properties, synthesis and characterization, processing methods and engineering 
application of polymers 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to polymers-Definition and classification of polymers, 
classification of polymer based on source, structure, application, thermal 
behaviour, mode of polymerization - natural and synthetic polymers, 
thermoplastics, thermosets, elastomers, basic concepts of polymerization 
(addition, condensation), Copolymerisation-Different types of copolymers-
Characteristics.  
8 
2 
Molecular weight of polymers – weight average and number average 
molecular weight – sedimentation and viscosity average molecular weights. 
Experimental methods for molecular weight determination – end group 
analysis, light scattering method – viscometry (Ostwald viscometer) intrinsic 
viscosity. Molecular weight distribution curve.  
Polymer properties - Polymer architecture (linear, branched, crosslinked, 
etc.), Crystallinity and glass transition temperature, Mechanical properties, 
(elasticity, viscoelasticity, yield), Thermal properties and degradation, 
Electrical and optical properties 
 
10 

 
Definition 
and 
applications 
of 
Polymer 
blends, 
composites 
and 
nanocomposites 
3 
Polymer Synthesis and characterization -step growth polymerization, 
chain growth polymerization, Methods of polymerization, copolymerization 
and copolymer types – bulk, solution, suspension and emulsion 
polymerization. 
Differential 
Scanning 
Calorimetry 
(DSC) 
and 
Thermogravimetric Analysis (TGA), applications of spectroscopic methods 
in polymer characterization 
8 
4 
Polymer processing and engineering applications-  
Plastic processing technology-injection moulding-compression moulding - 
calendaring – blow moulding – extrusion – thermoforming – wet, dry and 
melt spinning methods for fibres –vulcanization of rubber –– general study 
of elastomer processing - brief description of compounding methods. 
Applications in drug delivery, tissue engineering, and medical devices, 
conductive polymers and their applications, polymers in microelectronics 
and photonics, dielectric and insulating materials,  polymers in automotive 
and aerospace applications, polymer coatings and adhesives  
10

SEMESTER 6 
POLLUTION CONTROL IN PROCESS INDUSTRIES 
Course Code 
OECHT613 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3-0-0-0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. Provide a comprehensive understanding of environmental regulations and pollution 
control principles. 
2. Impart various technologies for wastewater treatment, sludge treatment and disposal, 
solid waste management strategies, air pollution management, and the abatement of 
noise& odour pollution to students. 
3. Equip students with knowledge about preventing pollution in various industries, 
understanding emerging environmental challenges posed by new technologies like 
biotechnology and nanotechnology, and analysing historical industrial disasters such 
as the Bhopal tragedy. 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Basics of Pollution Control - Environmental Regulations and Standards: 
National regulations, Key legislations. Pollution Control Strategies - End-of-
pipe treatments, Source reduction and waste minimization. 
Wastewater Pollution and Treatment Methods -  Sources and 
classification of wastewater- Types of water pollutants and their effects. 
Treatment methods(brief overview- diagram, principle and working of 
equipment only) - Physical Treatment Methods: Screening, grit removal, 
Sedimentation, 
flotation, 
filtration, 
Chemical 
Treatment 
Methods: 
Coagulation, flocculation, precipitation, Biological Treatment Methods: 
9  

 
Activated sludge, biofilm reactors, anaerobic digestion. 
2 
Sludge Treatment and Disposal - sludge thickening - sludge conditioning - 
sludge dewatering - sludge digestion and composting (brief overview). 
Solid Waste Treatment-sources and classification, disposal methods-open 
dumping, sanitary landfill, incineration-composting (brief overview). 
Noise pollution–Sources, effects of noise on people, noise control methods. 
9  
3 
Air Pollution: Units of measurement, sources, classification. Sampling and 
analysis of air pollutants, health effects of air pollution global warming and 
ozone depletion. 
Devices for Particulate Contaminants: Gravitational settling, Centrifugal 
Collectors, Wet Collectors, Fabric filters and Electrostatic Precipitators 
(ESP) Control Devices for Gaseous Contaminants: Adsorption, 
Absorption, Condensation, Combustion, Automobile Emission Control. 
Odour Pollution Management-  Sources, Health Impacts, Odour 
Measurement and Monitoring, control methods. 
9 
4 
Pollution Prevention Techniques: Generic water management techniques. 
Pollution prevention in the electronic Industry, Power generation industry, 
Electroplating industry, Fabricated metals products industry. 
EmergingPollution: Threats and Pollution Caused by Biotechnology and 
Nanotechnology. Application of biotechnology and nanotechnology in 
pollution Control. Threats and Pollution Caused by Renewable energy 
technologies (PV cells and batteries only included).  
Case study: Industrial pollution and disasters: Bhopal tragedy, Water 
pollution control and disposal of waste water in HPCL Refinery 
Vishakhapatnam. 
9 
Course Assessment Method 
(CIE: 40 marks ,  ESE: 60 marks) 
 
Continuous Internal Evaluation Marks (CIE):

SEMESTER S6 
ENERGY ENGINEERING AND MANAGEMENT   
Course Code 
OECHT614 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None/ 
(Course code) 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. The course makes the students understand the importance of energy 
conservation and the different methods employed for methods for 
harnessing different energy resources. 
2. Students may gain knowledge on Energy Auditing, Energy conservation, Waste Heat 
Recovery, Maintenance of Energy Systems, 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Introduction to Energy Conversion - Energy resources, 
Global and Indian scenario of energy resources and consumption, Impact of 
Energy on economy, Energy policies , development and environment.  
Conventional Energy conversion plants –Thermal, Hydro, and Nuclear 
power plants , Comparison, advantages and disadvantages, Combined cycle 
power plants, 
Energy from Hydrogen :- Hydrogen as a source of energy, Sources, 
hydrogen 
energy 
storage 
and 
transportation, Applications, 
Future 
perspectives. 
9 
2 
Solar energy- Solar thermal systems- Flat plate collectors- Focusing 
collectors- Applications of solar energy in India  
Ocean energy :- wave energy conversion, Ocean thermal energy conversion, 
10 

 
Tidal energy conversion.  
Wind energy- Types of windmills- Wind electric power generation- Wind 
power in India,   
Magneto hydrodynamics, Fuel cells : types , working of PEMFC. 
3 
Energy management and Energy audit  
Energy Management – Definitions and significance, Objectives, 
Characterizing of energy usage,  Energy Management program, Energy 
strategies and energy 
planning.  
Energy Audit – Types, Procedure and Techniques, understanding energy 
costs, Benchmarking, Energy performance, Optimum performance of 
existing facilities. 
8 
4 
Energy conservation – Principles , Cogeneration ,Waste heat recovery , 
Waste to Energy Technologies- Gasification, Pyrolysis, Fermentation, 
Anaerobic digestion: compressed biogas.  
Energy Conservation Opportunities – Electrical ECOs,  Thermodynamic 
ECOs in chemical process industry, ECOs  in residential and commercial 
buildings, Energy Conservation Measures. 
9

SEMESTER S6 
PETROLEUM REFINING TECHNOLOGY  
Course Code 
OECHT615 
CIE Marks 
40 
Teaching Hours/Week 
(L: T:P: R) 
3:0:0:0 
ESE Marks 
60 
Credits 
3 
Exam Hours 
2 Hrs. 30 Min. 
Prerequisites (if any) 
None 
Course Type 
Theory 
 
Course Objectives: 
1. To apply chemical engineering principles to design and analyze refinery processes.  
2. To gain knowledge of the various stages of crude oil refining, including distillation, 
cracking, and reforming. 
3. To provide students with a comprehensive understanding of the petrochemical 
industry, its processes, and the underlying principles 
 
SYLLABUS 
Module 
No. 
Syllabus Description 
Contact 
Hours 
1 
Origin and formation of crude oil: Oil exploration and drilling. Storage 
and transportation of crude oil and products. Classification, Composition and 
Evaluation of oil stock. Status of Petroleum industry in India. Classification 
of petroleum refinery. Preliminary petroleum processing-Impurities in crude 
oil, Dehydration and desalting of crude-Electric Desalter-, Process 
description, factors affecting the electric desalter. Pipe still furnaces and its 
operations. 
9  
2 
Distillation of crude- Prefractionator: Atmospheric topping unit, Vacuum 
distillation unit. Thermal Conversion process: Process description of 
Thermal cracking, Visbreaking, Coking. Process description of fluid 
Catalytic cracking unit, Hydro cracking. Process description of catalytic 
reforming. Process description of alkylation process- sulphuric acid 
9 

 
alkylation. Treatment of gasoline- Copper Chloride process and Merox 
sweetening. 
3 
Petrochemical Industries & their feed stocks: Process of Synthesis gas 
production by steam reforming of Naphtha, Manufacture of Methanol from 
Synthesis Gas, Production of liquid fuels from Synthesis gas by Fischer – 
Tropsch process.  
Petrochemical products and their applications: First, Second and Third 
generation petrochemical products, Production of Ethylene, Propylene, and 
Butadiene by Naphtha/Gas cracking, 
9 
4 
Plastomers, Elastomers and Synthetic fibres: Various methods of 
polymerization and their mechanisms, Production processes of LDPE, 
LLDPE and HDPE, Basic difference among the three and their applications, 
Production of PVC and Polystyrene, Production of Polypropylene, 
Production of SBR, PBR and Butyl rubber, Production of ABS plastics, 
Production of Polyamide (Nylon 6 and Nylon 6,6), Polyester and Acrylic 
fibres, Production of Phenol Formaldehyde resins, Detergents: Classification 
of detergents, Production of Linear Alkyl Benzene (LAB) from Superior 
Kerosene and Benzene, Sulphonation of LAB for production of Synthetic 
Detergents. Additives for synthetic detergents. Hard and soft detergents. 
9 
.
